## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T03:07:48Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/.claude/plugins/cache/claude-plugins-official/claude-md-management/1.0.0/skills/claude-md-improver

# CLAUDE.md Improver

Audit, evaluate, and improve CLAUDE.md files across a codebase to ensure Claude Code has optimal project context.

**This skill can write to CLAUDE.md files.** After presenting a quality report and getting user approval, it updates CLAUDE.md files with targeted improvements.

## Workflow

### Phase 1: Discovery

Find all CLAUDE.md files in the repository:

```bash
find . -name "CLAUDE.md" -o -name ".claude.md" -o -name ".claude.local.md" 2>/dev/null | head -50
```

**File Types & Locations:**

| Type | Location | Purpose |
|------|----------|---------|
| Project root | `./CLAUDE.md` | Primary project context (checked into git, shared with team) |
| Local overrides | `./.claude.local.md` | Personal/local settings (gitignored, not shared) |
| Global defaults | `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md` | User-wide defaults across all projects |
| Package-specific | `./packages/*/CLAUDE.md` | Module-level context in monorepos |
| Subdirectory | Any nested location | Feature/domain-specific context |

**Note:** Claude auto-discovers CLAUDE.md files in parent directories, making monorepo setups work automatically.

### Phase 2: Quality Assessment

For each CLAUDE.md file, evaluate against quality criteria. See [references/quality-criteria.md](references/quality-criteria.md) for detailed rubrics.

**Quick Assessment Checklist:**

| Criterion | Weight | Check |
|-----------|--------|-------|
| Commands/workflows documented | High | Are build/test/deploy commands present? |
| Architecture clarity | High | Can Claude understand the codebase structure? |
| Non-obvious patterns | Medium | Are gotchas and quirks documented? |
| Conciseness | Medium | No verbose explanations or obvious info? |
| Currency | High | Does it reflect current codebase state? |
| Actionability | High | Are instructions executable, not vague? |

**Quality Scores:**
- **A (90-100)**: Comprehensive, current, actionable
- **B (70-89)**: Good coverage, minor gaps
- **C (50-69)**: Basic info, missing key sections
- **D (30-49)**: Sparse or outdated
- **F (0-29)**: Missing or severely outdated

### Phase 3: Quality Report Output

**ALWAYS output the quality report BEFORE making any updates.**

Format:

```
## CLAUDE.md Quality Report

### Summary
- Files found: X
- Average score: X/100
- Files needing update: X

### File-by-File Assessment

#### 1. ./CLAUDE.md (Project Root)
**Score: XX/100 (Grade: X)**

| Criterion | Score | Notes |
|-----------|-------|-------|
| Commands/workflows | X/20 | ... |
| Architecture clarity | X/20 | ... |
| Non-obvious patterns | X/15 | ... |
| Conciseness | X/15 | ... |
| Currency | X/15 | ... |
| Actionability | X/15 | ... |

**Issues:**
- [List specific problems]

**Recommended additions:**
- [List what should be added]

#### 2. ./packages/api/CLAUDE.md (Package-specific)
...
```

### Phase 4: Targeted Updates

After outputting the quality report, ask user for confirmation before updating.

**Update Guidelines (Critical):**

1. **Propose targeted additions only** - Focus on genuinely useful info:
   - Commands or workflows discovered during analysis
   - Gotchas or non-obvious patterns found in code
   - Package relationships that weren't clear
   - Testing approaches that work
   - Configuration quirks

2. **Keep it minimal** - Avoid:
   - Restating what's obvious from the code
   - Generic best practices already covered
   - One-off fixes unlikely to recur
   - Verbose explanations when a one-liner suffices

3. **Show diffs** - For each change, show:
   - Which CLAUDE.md file to update
   - The specific addition (as a diff or quoted block)
   - Brief explanation of why this helps future sessions

**Diff Format:**

```markdown
### Update: ./CLAUDE.md

**Why:** Build command was missing, causing confusion about how to run the project.

```diff
+ ## Quick Start
+
+ ```bash
+ npm install
+ npm run dev  # Start development server on port 3000
+ ```
```
```

### Phase 5: Apply Updates

After user approval, apply changes using the Edit tool. Preserve existing content structure.

## Templates

See [references/templates.md](references/templates.md) for CLAUDE.md templates by project type.

## Common Issues to Flag

1. **Stale commands**: Build commands that no longer work
2. **Missing dependencies**: Required tools not mentioned
3. **Outdated architecture**: File structure that's changed
4. **Missing environment setup**: Required env vars or config
5. **Broken test commands**: Test scripts that have changed
6. **Undocumented gotchas**: Non-obvious patterns not captured

## User Tips to Share

When presenting recommendations, remind users:

- **`#` key shortcut**: During a Claude session, press `#` to have Claude auto-incorporate learnings into CLAUDE.md
- **Keep it concise**: CLAUDE.md should be human-readable; dense is better than verbose
- **Actionable commands**: All documented commands should be copy-paste ready
- **Use `.claude.local.md`**: For personal preferences not shared with team (add to `.gitignore`)
- **Global defaults**: Put user-wide preferences in `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`

## What Makes a Great CLAUDE.md

**Key principles:**
- Concise and human-readable
- Actionable commands that can be copy-pasted
- Project-specific patterns, not generic advice
- Non-obvious gotchas and warnings

**Recommended sections** (use only what's relevant):
- Commands (build, test, dev, lint)
- Architecture (directory structure)
- Key Files (entry points, config)
- Code Style (project conventions)
- Environment (required vars, setup)
- Testing (commands, patterns)
- Gotchas (quirks, common mistakes)
- Workflow (when to do what)

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T04:43:31Z

Three-fold cost:

1. **Orianna does a full fact-check per attempt.** Reads the plan, extracts every load-bearing claim, greps the repo for each anchor, resolves paths through the claim contract (now concern-as-root for `work` ‚Äî walks the workspace monorepo), composes findings. A 600-line ADR with dozens of path tokens is ~90‚Äì180s per pass.

2. **Each ADR needs multiple iterations.** Dashboard-tab took 4 commits before it flipped (fix ‚Üí re-sign ‚Üí new findings ‚Üí fix ‚Üí re-sign). Lifecycle, s1-s2, session-state each have similar cleanup surfaces ‚Äî legacy `tools/demo-studio-v3/` refs need `company-os/` requalification, URL-shaped tokens in backticks need suppressors, open questions need DEFERRED markers.

3. **Commit ceremony per fix.** Pre-commit hooks run (secret scan, structure check, tests for changed packages), pre-push hooks run. Each iteration is a full commit cycle.

So: 3 ADRs √ó ~3 iterations √ó ~2 min = ~18 min floor, plus fix-composition time in between. Ekko also has to read fact-check reports, reason about which fix category applies (requalify vs. DEFER vs. suppress), and preserve semantic integrity.

**Speedup options if you want to invest:**
- **Batch-fix pre-pass** ‚Äî one agent sweeps all 3 ADRs for the known finding categories (legacy `tools/` paths, URL-tokens, unresolved `?` markers) in a single pass before re-signing. Cuts iterations per ADR from ~3 to ~1.
- **Orianna prompt tuning** ‚Äî reduce over-citation in the prompt, batch anchor lookups. Bigger-scope change, not for today.
- **Pre-lint plans at author time** ‚Äî run a structural check before the author hands off, so the first sign attempt is cleaner. Planner-side discipline.

Per hands-off: nothing to action here ‚Äî Ekko is already on iteration 3-ish based on commit count. Speedup (a) would have helped if dispatched earlier; diminishing return now.

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T04:47:21Z

**Jayce done ‚Äî MAD.A phase green.** 8 xfail tests ‚Üí 8 passing. 2 commits local on branch, no push. AsyncTTLCache with asyncio single-flight lock + feature-flagged routes at request-time check. Two minor flags for you:

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:53:02Z

Can you propose a feedback to improve the speed? especially regarding orianna gate. Or did you already do that?

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:53:28Z

Already filed ‚Äî `feedback/2026-04-21-orianna-signing-latency.md` (commit `be98f9b`). Four options:

- **(a) Batch-fix pre-pass** ‚Äî one agent sweeps all queued ADRs for known finding categories (legacy `tools/` paths, URL-tokens, unresolved `?` markers) before any sign attempt. Cuts iterations/ADR from ~3 to ~1.
- **(b) Author-time pre-lint** ‚Äî planners run `check_plan_structure` + claim-contract pre-scan before handoff, so first sign is usually clean.
- **(c) Orianna prompt tuning** ‚Äî reduce over-citation, batch anchor lookups, cache claim-contract across iterations.
- **(d) Auto-requalify** ‚Äî `orianna-sign.sh` pre-pass rewrites known-safe workspace prefixes deterministically before invoking Orianna.

My recommendation there was: ship (a) as `scripts/orianna-pre-fix-work-adr.sh`; fold (b) into next planner-agent refresh; park (c)+(d).

**New failure modes this session surfaces that weren't in that doc** ‚Äî worth a follow-up feedback note:

1. **Body-edit ‚Üí sign invalidation is not a flagged gotcha anywhere upstream.** Yuumi inlined tasks on 3 ADRs in good faith; every downstream agent then had to reverse-promote (`approved` ‚Üí `proposed`), re-sign, re-promote. Ekko documented recovery in a learning, but it's a process landmine the toolchain could detect. Proposal: `orianna-verify-signature.sh` on pre-commit should error-loudly when the plan body hash differs from the hash the signature was computed against, pointing at the recovery procedure.

2. **Sign iterations serialize hard because of the commit-ceremony guard.** `pre-commit-orianna-signature-guard.sh` forces every signature commit to touch only the signature line ‚Äî meaning body fixes and signature ship in separate commits. Per-iteration: fix commit + Orianna re-run + sig-only commit. That doubles commit count. Proposal: allow a single atomic "signed fix" commit shape where the hook verifies the fix+sig commit is internally consistent.

3. **`.git/index.lock` recovery wastes a full Ekko dispatch.** Previous Ekko died mid-work with index held; next Ekko refused to touch it without permission. Proposal: sign script detects and auto-clears a lock older than 60s (with a loud audit log line), since Ekko is the only writer inside the script.

4. **Sibling `-tasks.md` file pattern vs ¬ßD3 one-plan-one-file rule was a latent mismatch.** Kayn/Aphelios authored separate task files (consistent with how some earlier ADRs shipped); Orianna in_progress gate enforces inline. Proposal: either Kayn/Aphelios always inline, or ¬ßD3 grants sibling `-tasks.md` as a recognized shape. Pick one, enforce at plan-structure-check time (pre-handoff), not at sign time.

Want me to file these four as a follow-up feedback doc? Or extend the existing one?

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:55:35Z

Proposal: orianna-verify-signature.sh
  on pre-commit should error-loudly when the plan body hash differs from the hash the
  signature was computed against, pointing at the recovery procedure can you explain more?

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:56:02Z

Sure. The mechanics:

**Current state.** `orianna-sign.sh` runs the full fact-check on the plan's body, then appends a signature block like this to the frontmatter:

```yaml
orianna_signature_approved:
  hash: 8f50da6‚Ä¶
  signed_at: 2026-04-21T05:42:00Z
  signer: orianna
```

That `hash` is a SHA of the plan body *at the moment Orianna signed it*. `scripts/orianna-verify-signature.sh` already exists and, when `plan-promote.sh` calls it, it recomputes the body hash and refuses to move the plan forward if the stored hash doesn't match. **So the signature invalidation IS detected ‚Äî but only at promotion time, not at commit time.**

The gap: nothing stops an agent (Yuumi, a planner, anyone) from editing a plan body that already carries a signature and committing the change. The invalidated signature sits quietly in the frontmatter. The next person who runs `plan-promote.sh` discovers it, then has to do the full recovery dance (revert the file back to `proposed/`, flip frontmatter `status:`, re-sign, re-promote). That's what burned two Ekko dispatches today.

**Proposal.** A pre-commit hook ‚Äî `scripts/hooks/orianna-body-hash-guard.sh` ‚Äî that for every plan file in the staged diff with a signature block, recomputes the body hash the same way `orianna-verify-signature.sh` does and compares it to the stored hash. On mismatch:

1. Block the commit with a loud message:
   ```
   ‚úò Plan body edited after signing:
     plans/approved/work/2026-04-20-managed-agent-lifecycle.md
     stored hash:   8f50da6‚Ä¶
     computed hash: a1b2c3d‚Ä¶
   
   Body edits invalidate the Orianna signature. To recover:
     1. git mv plans/approved/work/<plan>.md plans/proposed/work/
     2. Set `status: proposed` in frontmatter
     3. Commit ("chore: revert <slug> to proposed for re-sign after body edit")
     4. scripts/orianna-sign.sh <plan> approved
     5. scripts/plan-promote.sh <plan>
   
   Or, if you're mid-signing and this commit IS the re-sign: allow with
     git commit --trailer 'Orianna-Body-Edit-Acknowledged: <reason>'
   ```

2. Allow an explicit acknowledgement trailer for the case where the edit and re-sign are deliberate (Ekko mid-flow). The trailer is just a breadcrumb in commit history ‚Äî the next commit in the flow still has to carry a valid signature or the hook fires again.

**What this buys:**
- Shifts the failure from "discovered during `plan-promote.sh` after three unrelated commits have piled on" to "blocked at the moment of the mistake."
- Makes the recovery procedure self-documenting ‚Äî the error message IS the runbook.
- Zero cost on the happy path (hash recompute is ~ms per file).
- Doesn't require Orianna to run ‚Äî it's a pure cryptographic check. Fast.

**Caveats:**
- Need to confirm `orianna-verify-signature.sh` actually uses a reproducible body-hash scheme (canonical whitespace, stripped signature block, etc.). If it doesn't, this won't work without fixing that first.
- The trailer escape hatch needs scope ‚Äî should only be acceptable on commits where the only changed file is the plan itself (same rule as the existing `pre-commit-orianna-signature-guard.sh`).

Want me to write this up as a feedback doc or a plan?

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:58:20Z

Sign iterations serialize hard because of the commit-ceremony guard.
  pre-commit-orianna-signature-guard.sh forces every signature commit to touch only the
  signature line ‚Äî meaning body fixes and signature ship in separate commits. Per-iteration:
   fix commit + Orianna re-run + sig-only commit. That doubles commit count. Proposal: allow
   a single atomic "signed fix" commit shape where the hook verifies the fix+sig commit is
  internally consistent. can you explain more

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T06:58:52Z

Yes. This one's about commit ceremony, not hashing.

**Current state.** `pre-commit-orianna-signature-guard.sh` enforces a rule: **a commit that touches the `orianna_signature_*` block in a plan must touch *only* that block ‚Äî nothing else in the file, nothing in other files.** That protects against someone sneaking body edits into a signature commit (which would invalidate the signature they just wrote).

The rule is correct in intent. The cost is that the actual sign-iteration flow looks like this:

```
iteration N:
  1. orianna-sign.sh <plan> <phase>          ‚Üê Orianna finds findings, exits non-zero
  2. edit plan (add suppressors, requalify paths, LOCK/DEFER open questions)
  3. git commit -m "chore: orianna fixes for <slug> <phase>"   ‚Üê body-only commit
  4. orianna-sign.sh <plan> <phase>          ‚Üê re-run, clean (hopefully)
  5. git commit -m "chore: orianna signature for <slug>-<phase>"   ‚Üê sig-only commit
```

Two commits per successful iteration. Three iterations to clean sign = 6 commits per ADR per phase. Today's run: MAD + BD + MAL + SE √ó (approved + in_progress) √ó ~3 iterations = up to **36 commits just for signing**. Each commit fires pre-commit hooks (secret scan, structure check, package tests), pre-push hooks, commit-msg validators. That's where the ceremony drag compounds.

**Proposal.** Let the guard accept a single "signed fix" commit shape instead of forcing two. The hook would allow:

```
Allowed commit shapes for touching orianna_signature_<phase>:
  A. Signature-only: only the `orianna_signature_<phase>:` block changes.
  B. Signed-fix: body changes + orianna_signature_<phase>: block change, IF:
     - the commit carries a `Signed-Fix: <phase>` trailer
     - the computed body-hash AFTER the commit's applied diff matches the hash
       embedded in the new signature block
     - the only file touched is the plan itself
```

Shape B means: "I edited the body *and* wrote the new signature in the same commit, and here's the cryptographic proof that the new signature was computed against the post-edit body." The hook verifies that proof by running the same body-hash function `orianna-verify-signature.sh` uses, against the file content after the diff is applied.

**What this enables.** The `orianna-sign.sh` script can itself collapse the two-step ceremony: when it runs and finds findings that it's been told to auto-fix (e.g. the (a) batch-fix pre-pass or (d) auto-requalify options from the earlier feedback), it applies the fix and writes the signature in one operation, then commits with the `Signed-Fix:` trailer. Same audit trail, half the commits, half the hook runs, half the wall time.

**Why the invariant still holds.** The guard's original goal ‚Äî prevent sneaked-in body edits from coexisting with a signature ‚Äî is preserved. It's just enforced cryptographically (hash-match) rather than structurally (no other changed lines). Cryptographic enforcement is actually *stronger*: under the current rule, someone could legitimately change "one character in a suppressor comment" and the hook wouldn't care, because it only checks which lines changed. Under the hash-match rule, *any* body change that isn't reflected in the new signature's hash fails.

**Caveats & cost.**
- Requires the body-hash function to be deterministic and reproducible (same caveat as the previous proposal ‚Äî they share this dependency).
- The `Signed-Fix:` trailer is a soft signal; the hash check is what actually enforces. Trailer only exists so humans reviewing the log can grep for fix-and-sign commits separately from pure sig commits.
- Doesn't help iterations that genuinely require multiple Orianna runs (e.g. fix finding A ‚Üí Orianna now surfaces finding B that was masked by A). Those still take multiple rounds, but each round is now 1 commit instead of 2.
- Orianna's own runtime (~90‚Äì180s per fact-check pass) is unchanged. This only removes commit ceremony overhead, which on today's run was probably 5‚Äì15s per commit √ó 30+ commits = meaningful but not dominant. Still worth doing because it stacks with (a) and (d).

Shape: small shell script change to the guard, modest contract change to `orianna-sign.sh`. Want a feedback doc or a plan?

Ok please put all of these into the feedback, and we will fix this

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T07:10:56Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

Path forward per your "use admin to promote all plans" ‚Äî **you run the bypass commits under your admin identity**. Here's the paste-ready block. Local git config is still `Duongntd`; env-var override per commit works under your actual admin session (not agent spoofing).

```bash
cd /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents

# Per-commit admin identity
export GIT_AUTHOR_NAME="harukainguyen1411"
export GIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL="harukainguyen1411@gmail.com"
export GIT_COMMITTER_NAME="harukainguyen1411"
export GIT_COMMITTER_EMAIL="harukainguyen1411@gmail.com"

# Helper to commit with Orianna-Bypass trailer via COMMIT_EDITMSG
# (Apple Git 2.39.5 doesn't pre-populate COMMIT_EDITMSG on -m, so we -F)
fastlane() {
  local slug="$1" from_dir="$2" to_dir="$3" from_status="$4" to_status="$5"
  local src="plans/${from_dir}/work/${slug}.md"
  local dst="plans/${to_dir}/work/${slug}.md"
  git mv "$src" "$dst"
  sed -i '' "s/^status: ${from_status}\$/status: ${to_status}/" "$dst"
  git add "$src" "$dst"
  cat > "$(git rev-parse --git-dir)/COMMIT_EDITMSG" <<EOF
chore: fastlane-promote ${slug} to ${to_status}

Admin-bypass ship-day fastlane. Impl status tracked on feature branches;
this lifecycle bump is administrative to unblock downstream workflows.

Orianna-Bypass: admin ship-day fastlane ‚Äî signing ceremony cost disproportionate at this phase; impl verified on integration branches
EOF
  git commit -F "$(git rev-parse --git-dir)/COMMIT_EDITMSG"
}

# E2E ship: approved ‚Üí in-progress
fastlane 2026-04-21-demo-studio-v3-e2e-ship approved in-progress approved in-progress

# Four impl ADRs: in-progress ‚Üí implemented
fastlane 2026-04-20-managed-agent-dashboard-tab in-progress implemented in-progress implemented
fastlane 2026-04-20-managed-agent-lifecycle    in-progress implemented in-progress implemented
fastlane 2026-04-20-s1-s2-service-boundary     in-progress implemented in-progress implemented
fastlane 2026-04-20-session-state-encapsulation in-progress implemented in-progress implemented

# Claim-contract: in-progress ‚Üí implemented
fastlane 2026-04-21-orianna-claim-contract-work-repo-prefixes in-progress implemented in-progress implemented

unset GIT_AUTHOR_NAME GIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL GIT_COMMITTER_NAME GIT_COMMITTER_EMAIL

# Verify
ls plans/approved/work/ plans/in-progress/work/ plans/implemented/work/
git log --oneline -7
```

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T08:46:10Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

Lissandra running. Waiting on sentinel + commit.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Strawberry Sona (work-concern) coordinator protocol; delegates to Sonnet subagents.
   - Plan lifecycle: proposed ‚Üí approved ‚Üí in-progress ‚Üí implemented. Pre-commit `plan-promote-guard.sh` only fires on `proposed ‚Üí *`; later transitions unguarded by hook but `plan-promote.sh` would enforce signatures.
   - Critical Rule #19: Orianna signature gate on every transition; bypass only via `Orianna-Bypass:` trailer from `harukainguyen1411@gmail.com` admin identity. Agent-identity bypass = Content Integrity / Impersonation violation.
   - `integration/demo-studio-v3-waves-1-4` branch, tracked via worktree named `company-os-integration/` ‚Äî misleading naming, worktree != branch name.
   - Apple Git 2.39.5 quirk: `git commit -m` does NOT pre-populate `.git/COMMIT_EDITMSG` before pre-commit hooks fire. Workaround: `cat > $(git rev-parse --git-dir)/COMMIT_EDITMSG <<EOF...EOF && git commit -F`.
   - `pre-commit-zz-plan-structure.sh` blocks cross-repo backtick paths; suppressor syntax `<!-- orianna: ok -->` per line.
   - `GIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL` / `GIT_COMMITTER_EMAIL` env vars override local git config for single commit; hook reads `GIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL` first.
   - Python balanced-paren regex for stripping multi-line `@pytest.mark.xfail(...)` decorators (naive `[^)]*` fails on nested parens in `reason=(...)`).
   - Conftest module stubbing: `sys.modules.setdefault("anthropic", _stub)` ‚Äî exception classes referenced in `except` clauses must exist on stub because Python evaluates except-clause types on every raise.
   - `transition_status(session_id, new_status, *, cancel_reason: str | None = None)` ‚Äî kwarg-only cross-ADR contract per OQ-MAL-6 / SE.A.6.
   - Bash-deny pattern this session: builder-role specific (Viktor, Jayce) vs tester/advisor/executor (Vi, Rakan, Ekko, Heimerdinger all fine).

### 2. Boot the FastAPI app locally
```bash

uvicorn main:app --reload --port 8080
```
Then hit endpoints with `curl` or the Swagger UI at `http://localhost:8080/docs`.

### 3. Exercise the new MAD routes
- **List managed sessions** (MAD.B):
  ```bash
  curl http://localhost:8080/managed-sessions
  ```
  Observe: enrichment join, TTL cache behavior (second call within TTL should be faster / hit cache).

- **Terminate a managed session** (MAD.C.1):
  ```bash
  curl -X POST http://localhost:8080/managed-sessions/<id>/terminate
  ```
  Observe idempotency: second call on a terminated session returns 200 (anthropic.NotFoundError ‚Üí idempotent pass).

### 4. Exercise the dashboard UI (MAD.D)
If the demo-studio-v3 frontend has a dev server (check `package.json`), run it and visit the managed-agent dashboard tab. Confirm list rendering + terminate button + refresh behavior against the local FastAPI backend.

Unit-test exercise already covered by pytest, but if you want manual: drive `transition_status(session_id, "cancelled", cancel_reason="user-abort")` from a Python REPL against the dev Firestore to see the terminal-state cleanup hook + SE encapsulation path.

```bash
cd ~/Documents/Work/mmp/workspace/company-os-integration
git checkout chore/ship-day-deploy-infra -- scripts/deploy/rollback.sh
bash scripts/deploy/rollback.sh --dry-run   # or inspect without running
```

Just running `pytest` from `tools/demo-studio-v3` is the single highest-signal test. If it's green modulo the 2 known xfails, MAD/MAL/BD/SE impl is baseline-verified.

## Honest end-user answer

**Nothing is shipped to a URL you can visit.** The integration branch is not deployed to staging or prod. If you want to *use* the product right now, the only path is local.

### Local end-user flow (if it exists at all)
`demo-studio-v3` is a FastAPI + frontend tool. To "use it as an end user":

```bash
cd ~/Documents/Work/mmp/workspace/company-os-integration
git checkout integration/demo-studio-v3-waves-1-4
cd tools/demo-studio-v3
uvicorn main:app --reload --port 8080
# then open http://localhost:8080 (or /docs for the API)
```

**Caveats that will bite you:**
1. **Firestore.** The app talks to real Firestore in prod. Locally it'll either need emulator config or real GCP creds. The tests stub `google.cloud.firestore` ‚Äî the app at runtime does not.
2. **Anthropic API.** Terminate / session creation hit real Anthropic. Needs `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. Tests stub it; app does not.
3. **Slack integration.** The configure/approve flow is Slack-triggered. Without the Slack app wired, you can't drive the full session lifecycle from a user's perspective ‚Äî only poke endpoints directly with curl.
4. **Frontend dev server.** I haven't verified whether `tools/demo-studio-v3` has a Vue/React frontend served separately or if FastAPI serves static. If it's separate, you need to run its dev server too.
5. **Managed-session monitor + dashboard feature flag.** `MANAGED_AGENT_DASHBOARD=false` was shipped dormant in the deploy env vars. For local testing flip it to `true` in your env.

### Realistic end-user readiness per ADR
| ADR | End-user visible | Local-usable | Staged | Prod |
|-----|------------------|--------------|--------|------|
| MAD (dashboard tab) | ‚úÖ UI exists | üü° with frontend+firestore+anthropic setup | ‚ùå | ‚ùå |
| MAL (lifecycle) | üü° backend only | üü° via API calls | ‚ùå | ‚ùå |
| BD (service boundary) | ‚ùå internal | N/A | ‚ùå | ‚ùå |
| SE (session state) | ‚ùå internal | N/A | ‚ùå | ‚ùå |

### Bottom line
- **Can you use it?** Technically yes, locally, if you wire Firestore + Anthropic + Slack creds. Realistically, no ‚Äî not in a "click and demo" sense.
- **The shortest path to a clickable product is the ship sequence:** Vi audit ‚Üí merge deploy-infra ‚Üí stg deploy ‚Üí smoke ‚Üí stg URL you can open in a browser.
- Staging is **one Vi greenlight + one Cloud Run deploy** away. That's probably ~15‚Äì30 min of work from now if the audit comes back clean.

## Yes ‚Äî you can run this locally end-to-end right now

There's a proper local-run path already built into demo-studio-v3. No coordinator work needed to make it go.

### Recipe (what you do)

```bash
cd ~/Documents/Work/mmp/workspace/company-os-integration/tools/demo-studio-v3
git status  # confirm on integration/demo-studio-v3-waves-1-4 @ bda562e

# 1. Deps (once)
pip install -r requirements.txt

# 2. Create .env from Bitwarden
#    ‚Üí open Bitwarden Dev collection ‚Üí "demo-studio-v3 local env"
#    ‚Üí paste values into a new file .env in this dir
#    Required keys per README:
#      ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, WALLET_STUDIO_BASE_URL, WALLET_STUDIO_API_KEY,
#      FIRESTORE_PROJECT_ID, SESSION_SECRET, INTERNAL_SECRET,
#      DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_TOKEN, COOKIE_SECURE=false,
#      MANAGED_AGENT_ID, MANAGED_ENVIRONMENT_ID, MANAGED_VAULT_ID

# 3. Add these to .env for the new wiring
echo "MANAGED_AGENT_DASHBOARD=1" >> .env     # show MAD tab (default off)
echo "MANAGED_SESSION_MONITOR_ENABLED=false" >> .env  # keep scanner off locally ‚Äî it'll terminate your sessions
echo "CONFIG_MGMT_URL=https://demo-config-mgmt-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app" >> .env
echo "FACTORY_URL=https://demo-factory-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app" >> .env
echo "CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN=..." >> .env          # from Secret Manager DS_CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN

# 4. Boot
source .env && bash scripts/run-backend.sh
# ‚Üí uvicorn on :8080 with auto-reload
```

### What you'll actually be able to exercise

| Surface | Works locally? | How to hit |
|---------|----------------|-----------|
| `/dashboard` (Sessions tab) | ‚úÖ | Browser: `http://localhost:8080/dashboard` |
| `/dashboard` (Managed Agents tab ‚Äî MAD) | ‚úÖ with `MANAGED_AGENT_DASHBOARD=1` | Same URL, click the new tab |
| `GET /api/managed-sessions` | ‚úÖ | Shows live Anthropic managed sessions + enrichment join (S2 brand fetch) |
| `POST /api/managed-sessions/{id}/terminate` | ‚úÖ | Per-row Stop button; hits real Anthropic |
| Session create via `/session/new` | ‚úÖ but normally Slack-triggered | Curl directly; auth guards may reject without INTERNAL_SECRET header |
| Full happy-path (Slack `/demo` ‚Üí agent configures ‚Üí build ‚Üí completed) | üü° partial | The Slack entry point needs slack-relay pointing at localhost (tunnel). But you can drive the lifecycle by creating a session via curl + calling `set_config` via demo-studio-mcp directly |
| MAL terminal hook (eager cleanup on `completed`) | ‚úÖ | Drive a session to `completed` via `/session/{id}/complete` or direct Firestore; watch the Anthropic session delete |
| MAL scanner (idle warn/terminate) | ‚ùå locally | Keep disabled; `MANAGED_SESSION_MONITOR_ENABLED=false` |
| BD thin `/build` call to S3 | ‚öÝÔ∏è live | Will hit prod S3 `demo-factory-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app` ‚Äî real build. Only do this with a throwaway test session. **OQ-SHIP-2 unconfirmed** (self-fetch). If S3 doesn't self-fetch, your build will fail for lack of config. |

### The sharp edges ‚Äî know before you run

1. **Firestore is real.** `FIRESTORE_PROJECT_ID=mmpt-233505` with `FIRESTORE_DATABASE=demo-studio-staging` from the deploy.sh default hits **live staging Firestore**. Any session you create lives there. Use a throwaway sessionId. If you'd rather isolate, point at an emulator (`FIRESTORE_EMULATOR_HOST=localhost:8080` + `gcloud emulators firestore start`).
2. **Anthropic managed sessions cost $.** Terminate what you create; the local MAL terminal hook fires on `completed`/`cancelled` transitions but not if you abandon the process. MAL scanner is off, so nothing will auto-clean for you.
3. **SE.C migration not run.** Existing rows in staging Firestore may have legacy enum values (`approved`/`complete`/`failed`/`archived`). The dashboard list still renders them, but MAL terminal-hook logic won't fire against them. New sessions you create locally will use the new enum. Not a blocker, just a quirk.
4. **S3 build call is live against prod factory.** Don't trigger `/build` on a session pointing at a real brand unless you want a real factory run. Use a throwaway brand name.
5. **Slack entry is not plug-and-play.** If you want the full Slack `/demo` ‚Üí config ‚Üí build flow, you need slack-relay pointed at your localhost via a tunnel (ngrok/cloudflared). For just exercising the dashboard + terminate + lifecycle ‚Äî no Slack needed.

### Fastest "does it work" check (no Slack, no build)

1. Boot backend.
2. Open `http://localhost:8080/dashboard`, click **Managed Agents** tab.
3. You should see rows for every currently-live Anthropic managed session on the account, with brand enrichment from S2 where available, `‚Äî ORPHAN` for ones not in Firestore, `‚Äî` for cold rows.
4. Click **Stop** on a throwaway row ‚Üí confirmation modal ‚Üí confirm ‚Üí row disappears on next 10s refresh.

That's MAD + MAL.A wrapper + SE.A.6 transition_status all exercised end-to-end against real Anthropic + real S2 + real Firestore. If that works, you've validated the core of the wiring.

**You're not blocked. Pull Bitwarden creds, add the 3 new env vars, run `scripts/run-backend.sh`.**

35af5b9da1d64a168d56507dd5a5d733 I can't call get_schema

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:04:40Z

I need more signal to diagnose. The session ID alone doesn't tell me where the call is breaking.

### What I know about `get_schema`
- It's an **MCP tool** exposed by `demo-studio-mcp` (TypeScript server), **not** an S1 route.
- Call chain: Anthropic managed agent ‚Üí `demo-studio-mcp` ‚Üí `GET /v1/schema` on S2 (`demo-config-mgmt-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app`).
- Auth: `DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_TOKEN` (agent ‚Üî MCP) + `CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN` (MCP ‚Üî S2).
- Per `setup_agent.py` the agent is hard-required to call `get_schema` as its **first** tool call in the GENERATE phase. If this fails, the whole session stalls.

### I need from you

1. **Where is the error surfacing?**
   - In the Anthropic agent transcript? (the agent says "tool returned error")
   - In your local `uvicorn` logs? (S1 got a 5xx back from somewhere)
   - In the MCP server logs? (demo-studio-mcp can't reach S2)
2. **Exact error text** ‚Äî HTTP status, body, any traceback. Even one line helps.

That's why the agent sees a persistent fetch failure and loops through retries ‚Äî its MCP endpoint is returning 503 at the transport layer before it can even reach S2.

### Why this is pre-existing / infra-level, not a ship-day regression

From `docs/cloud-run-config-snapshot.md`:
- **Image registry**: `europe-west1-docker.pkg.dev/ds-v3-workspace-2026/...` ‚Äî source project marked *deleted*.

The MCP service's backing project was torn down. If Cloud Run cold-started a new instance it would fail to pull the image (project gone). That matches a 503.

S2 (`demo-config-mgmt`) is fine ‚Äî returns 401 without token, which is correct behavior (service up, needs auth).

This is a **Heimerdinger** job, not a coordinator Bash job. One of:

3. **Point `DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_URL`** in your `.env` at the newly deployed URL.
4. Retry the session ‚Äî the agent will be able to call `get_schema`.

Dispatch Heimerdinger to run this? It's a ~20‚Äì40 min errand depending on whether the source project teardown left any image rebuild work.

### What each one is for

| Service | Role | Talks to |
|---------|------|----------|
| **S1 `demo-studio`** | HTTP backend for the *browser UI* + Slack entry + session lifecycle + dashboard | Firestore (sessions), Anthropic (managed-session create/stop), S2 (fetch_schema/fetch_config for UI enrichment), S3 (thin build trigger) |
| **`demo-studio-mcp`** | MCP server for the *agent's tool calls* ‚Äî how the LLM actually does anything | S2 for all config ops; returns results to the agent |
| **S2 `demo-config-mgmt`** | Config storage + schema authority | Firestore (configs) |
| **S3 `demo-factory-cloud`** | Runs the 11-step wallet factory | S2 (self-fetch per BD), Wallet Studio API |

The **BD ADR** specifically pulled config-translation out of S1 so that the MCP (not S1) is now the one-stop for agent-facing config ops. That's why *both* need to be running: the user talks to S1 (the browser dashboard,

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:08:22Z

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:08:22Z

Why? why can't our BE be the mcp server??

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:09:02Z

Honest answer: **there's no hard technical reason it can't.** It's a design choice, and arguably not the best one. Let me lay out why it's split today and why merging is reasonable.

### Why it's split today

1. **Language split (historical).** `demo-studio-mcp` is TypeScript/Node; S1 is Python/FastAPI. When the MCP server was authored, the MCP SDK was TS-first and the config schema types were shared with the TS-based MCP ecosystem. Python MCP SDK came later.
2. **BD boundary (current).** The BD ADR's thesis is "S1 = session lifecycle + agent hosting only; config logic lives elsewhere." The MCP server is where the agent's config-manipulation tools live, so putting them in a separate process kept that boundary physical, not just logical.
3. **Independent deploy / scale.** MCP is stateless and request-rate scales with agent tool-call chatter. S1 has session-lifetime state, SSE streams to browsers, Slack handling ‚Äî different scale profile.
4. **Auth separation.** The agent authenticates to MCP with `DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_TOKEN` from the Anthropic vault. S1 authenticates browser operators with cookies and Slack with `INTERNAL_SECRET`. Two processes = two auth postures can't cross-contaminate.

### Why "merge them" is reasonable

None of the above reasons are load-bearing. Specifically:

1. **Python MCP SDK exists now** (`mcp` package on PyPI). FastAPI can serve MCP over HTTP/SSE on a sub-route like `/mcp`. Anthropic's `mcp_servers=[{type: "url", url: "<S1-url>/mcp"}]` would route the agent there.
2. **BD boundary is about code organization, not process count.** You can keep the "config-translation lives in a distinct module" rule while hosting that module in S1's process. The grep-gate would still catch re-introduction of translation into the wrong module.
3. **One deploy is simpler than two.** Today's breakage is the perfect example: MCP 503 = whole system dead, but you have to diagnose a separate service. Merged, it's one log stream, one revision to roll back.
4. **One token, one secret to rotate.** Today `DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_TOKEN` lives in three places (Secret Manager, Anthropic vault, MCP env). Merged, you can use `INTERNAL_SECRET` with a sub-scope.

### What merging would cost

1. **Rewrite the MCP tool handlers in Python.** Not trivial ‚Äî the TS MCP server has the full `get_schema`/`get_config`/`set_config`/`trigger_factory`/`web_search` logic. Estimate: a few days of focused work, not a long project.
2. **Re-run `setup_agent.py --force`** to update the Anthropic-side `mcp_servers[0].url` to S1's URL + issue a new vault credential. One-shot errand.
3. **Blast radius.** S1 outages would take down both browser UI and agent tool-calls together. Today a 503 on MCP is bad but doesn't kill the dashboard. Post-merge, a bug in the dashboard layer could kill an in-progress agent session. Arguably acceptable given the whole system is already coupled.
4. **Re-evaluate BD.** BD's ¬ß3.14 delete-from-S1 list was motivated partly by the assumption that S1 doesn't *need* to know the schema. A merged MCP would mean S1 does need to know it again (at least in a submodule). The grep-gate would need a scoped allowlist.

### My read

If you're starting this over today, **one Python service serving FastAPI + MCP on the same process** is the cleaner architecture for a team of your size. Two services is worth it when you have two teams, two deploy cadences, or real scale asymmetry ‚Äî you have none of those.

The reason today is inertia + the BD ADR memorialized the split as an intentional boundary. Both are revisitable. Whether it's worth the port cost right now depends on how much more you plan to build on this ‚Äî if demo-studio-v4 is imminent, merge; if it's stable-maintenance, keep the split and just redeploy the MCP.

Want me to file this as a design assessment at `assessments/work/` so it's on the table for the next architecture pass? Or keep pushing on just getting the MCP service alive for today's ship?

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:14:35Z

Here's the happy-path flow in plain terms.

---

### 1. User kicks off a session (Slack)
**You type `/demo brand=Allianz market=DE` in Slack.**

- **Slack** posts to **S1** (`POST /session/new`).
- **S1** writes a bare row to **Firestore** (`demo-studio-sessions/{sessionId}`): just `status=configuring`, Slack thread info, no config yet.
- **S1** asks **Anthropic** to spin up a managed agent for this session. Anthropic returns a `managedSessionId`; S1 stores it on the Firestore row.
- **S1** replies to Slack with a chat link. You click it ‚Üí browser opens the studio UI on S1.

**State:** session exists, agent is booted, no config anywhere yet.

---

### 2. Agent figures out what to build (browser chat)
**You chat with the agent in the browser ("make it look like Allianz pet insurance").**

- Browser messages stream to **S1**, which relays them to the **Anthropic managed agent**.
- The agent calls MCP tools via **`demo-studio-mcp`**:
  - `get_schema` ‚Üí fetches the config schema shape from **S2** (`demo-config-mgmt`).
  - `web_search` ‚Üí researches Allianz brand (colors, logos, persona).
  - `set_config` ‚Üí writes the config (brand colors, copy, images) to **S2**, version 1.
- S1 is **not** in the config path ‚Äî MCP talks to S2 directly. S1 just streams chat.

**State:** a real config exists in S2 for this session. S1 still just has the lifecycle row.

---

### 3. You approve ‚Üí build starts
**You click "Build" in the UI.**

- Browser ‚Üí **S1** (`POST /session/{id}/build`).
- S1 flips the Firestore row: `configuring ‚Üí building` (via `transition_status`).
- S1 calls **S3 (`demo-factory-cloud`)** with just `{sessionId}` ‚Äî no config payload. Thin handoff.
- S3 fetches the config from S2 itself, then runs the 11-step factory pipeline (Wallet Studio project creation, assets, copy, pushes, cards, etc.).
- S3 calls back to S1 with status events as it progresses; S1 relays them to the browser over SSE so you see live progress.

**State:** Wallet Studio project is being generated.

---

### 4. QC runs, build completes
- S3 finishes ‚Üí calls S1 ‚Üí status transitions `building ‚Üí built ‚Üí qc_passed ‚Üí completed`.
- **On `completed`, MAL's terminal hook fires:** S1 tells Anthropic to delete the managed agent (so you stop paying for an idle session). Cost is bounded.
- Browser shows the preview iframe (served by S5 `demo-preview`) and the download / share links.

**State:** session is done. Managed agent is gone. Config lives in S2. Wallet project lives in Wallet Studio.

---

### 5. Operator visibility (dashboard)
**You open `/dashboard`, click the Managed Agents tab.**

- Browser ‚Üí **S1** `GET /api/managed-sessions`.
- S1 asks **Anthropic** for the list of currently-live managed sessions.
- For each row, S1 does two enrichment calls in parallel:
  - **Firestore** `batch_get_by_managed_ids` ‚Äî pulls Slack user, channel, lifecycle status for sessions we know about.
  - **S2** `fetch_config(sessionId)` ‚Äî pulls brand for display.
- Response is cached 10s. Tab auto-refreshes every 10s.

You see: every live agent, who owns it, what brand it's configured for, how long it's been idle, with a **Stop** button per row.

---

### 6. Manual cleanup (dashboard)
**Row looks orphaned or idle-forever. You click Stop.**

- Confirm modal ‚Üí **S1** `POST /api/managed-sessions/{id}/terminate`.
- S1 tells **Anthropic** to stop the managed session.
- If the session is in Firestore, S1 flips it to `cancelled` with `cancelReason=manual_dashboard`.
- Audit log entry written. List cache invalidated. Row disappears on next refresh.

---

### 7. Automated cleanup (background scanner)
**Some session ran for 60 min without activity.** (Scanner runs in S1 every 5 min.)

- Scanner fetches live sessions from Anthropic + their Firestore metadata.
- For each idle session:
  - 60 min idle ‚Üí posts a **slack warning** to `#demo-studio-alerts` via slack-relay.
  - 120 min idle ‚Üí terminates the managed agent + flips Firestore to `cancelled` with `cancelReason=idle_timeout`.

(Currently shipped with `MANAGED_SESSION_MONITOR_ENABLED=false` ‚Äî dormant until you flip it on.)

---

### The services, one-line each

| Who | What |
|-----|------|
| **Slack** | Entry point. `/demo` slash command. |
| **S1 `demo-studio`** | Lifecycle manager + browser UI + dashboard. Owns Firestore sessions. Thin handoffs to S3, Anthropic, slack-relay. |
| **`demo-studio-mcp`** | Agent's toolbox. Schema, config read/write, web search, build trigger. Talks to S2. |
| **S2 `demo-config-mgmt`** | Stores configs per sessionId. Single source of truth for "what are we building". |
| **S3 `demo-factory-cloud`** | Runs the 11-step Wallet Studio build. Self-fetches config from S2. |
| **S5 `demo-preview`** | Renders the preview iframe for the built project. |
| **Wallet Studio** | The actual product being configured. |
| **Anthropic** | Hosts the managed agent. |
| **Firestore** | Session lifecycle state. |
| **slack-relay** | Outbound Slack messaging (alerts). |

**Shortest answer to "what's an e2e flow":** Slack ‚Üí S1 boots an Anthropic agent ‚Üí agent uses `demo-studio-mcp` to configure via S2 ‚Üí user approves ‚Üí S1 triggers S3 ‚Üí S3 builds ‚Üí S1 marks complete and cleans up. Dashboard + scanner exist to catch sessions that don't finish cleanly.

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:30:28Z

do we really need mcp server or can we just use raw API for the managed agent?

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:31:35Z

Real question. Short answer: **probably not, if the user is always in the loop**.

### Why MCP exists in the current architecture

Managed agents run **autonomously in Anthropic's cloud**. Once spun up, there's no client pumping the tool-use/tool-result cycle ‚Äî Anthropic does it internally. That means tool execution has to happen somewhere Anthropic can reach on its own. Two places qualify:

1. **Anthropic-hosted tools** (`web_search`, `bash`, `computer`, `text_editor`) ‚Äî Anthropic runs these in the managed environment.
2. **MCP servers** ‚Äî Anthropic fetches your MCP URL and invokes tools there.

"Raw HTTP tools" aren't a third option in the managed-agent model. They would require a client in the loop to execute them, which defeats the managed-agent premise.

### Three realistic alternatives to MCP

| Option | How it works | Trade-off |
|--------|--------------|-----------|
| **A. Merge MCP into S1 process** | Python MCP SDK as a FastAPI sub-route (`/mcp`). Same managed-agent model. One deploy. | Still MCP protocol, but only one service to operate. |
| **B. Bash + curl via system prompt** | Give the managed agent only `bash` + `web_search` + `text_editor`. System prompt says "to update config, run `curl -X POST ...`". | Brittle. Agent invents wrong URLs, forgets tokens, 30% of runs fail on silly syntax. Security: bash has full internet access. Not real. |
| **C. Ditch managed agent entirely ‚Üí vanilla Messages API with client-side tools** | S1 holds a per-session conversation. On each user message, calls `messages.create` with `tools=[{name: "get_schema"}, {name: "set_config"}, ...]`. When response has `tool_use`, S1 executes it directly against S2 in-process, feeds `tool_result` back, streams text to browser over SSE. | **No MCP. No managed-agent. Simplest code.** |

### Why C is the honest answer for your flow

Your described flow has the user **always in the browser chatting**. There's no "agent runs for an hour while user is offline" scenario. That's exactly the case where managed agents' benefits are wasted:

- **Managed-agent benefit: asynchronous runs.** ‚Üí Not needed; user is synchronous.
- **Managed-agent benefit: sandboxed environment (computer-use).** ‚Üí Not needed; agent isn't running shell commands.
- **Managed-agent benefit: Anthropic web_search.** ‚Üí Available to the vanilla API too (`tools: [{type: "web_search_20241022"}]`).
- **Managed-agent cost: MCP server + vault + agent-creation flow + managed-session lifecycle + monitor + dashboard** ‚Üí All of MAL, MAD, and the MCP service exist *only because you chose managed-agent*.

If you switch to **vanilla Messages API + client-side tool calls**:
- MCP service goes away. (`demo-studio-mcp` deleted.)
- **MAL goes away.** No managed sessions to track or terminate.
- **MAD goes away.** No "managed sessions dashboard" ‚Äî just "active chat sessions" which is already in the Sessions tab.
- `setup_agent.py`, `.agent-ids.env`, `MANAGED_AGENT_ID`/`ENVIRONMENT_ID`/`VAULT_ID` ‚Äî gone.
- The Anthropic vault, `DEMO_STUDIO_MCP_TOKEN` ‚Äî gone.
- Auth posture simplifies: `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` only.

The code in S1 becomes:

```python
# Per-session conversation state (in Firestore or memory)
messages = load_conversation(session_id)
messages.append({"role": "user", "content": user_text})

while True:
    resp = await anthropic.messages.create(
        model="claude-sonnet-4-6",
        messages=messages,
        tools=[get_schema_tool, get_config_tool, set_config_tool, trigger_factory_tool, web_search_tool],
        system=SYSTEM_PROMPT,
    )
    messages.append({"role": "assistant", "content": resp.content})
    if resp.stop_reason == "end_turn":
        break
    # Execute tool_use blocks
    tool_results = []
    for block in resp.content:
        if block.type == "tool_use":
            result = await execute_tool(block.name, block.input, session_id)
            tool_results.append({"type": "tool_result", "tool_use_id": block.id, "content": result})
    messages.append({"role": "user", "content": tool_results})

save_conversation(session_id, messages)
```

`execute_tool` is just a switch calling `config_mgmt_client.fetch_schema()`, `config_mgmt_client.set_config()`, etc. ‚Äî the exact Python code S1 already has.

### What you lose

1. **Anthropic runs the loop for you.** With vanilla API, S1 is responsible for handling long tool-call chains, retries, timeouts. In practice for a chat-bounded flow this is ~50 lines.
2. **Thinking/reasoning steps visible to Anthropic's trace UI.** Managed agents show up in Anthropic's console; vanilla API calls don't.
3. **If tomorrow you want the agent to "keep working overnight on research"**, vanilla API can't do that without building polling infra. Managed agents can.

For demo-studio's use case ‚Äî synchronous human-in-the-loop config chat ‚Äî none of those matter.

### Sideways-answering your literal question

**If you want to keep managed agents** ‚Äî then yes, you need MCP (or Anthropic-hosted tools that happen to do what you need). Raw API is not an option in the managed-agent model.

**If you don't need managed agents** ‚Äî which I think you don't, based on the flow ‚Äî vanilla Messages API is a much simpler architecture. No MCP, no MAL, no MAD, no vault. Major code deletion. Probably a day or two of work to port.

Want me to dispatch a design assessment comparing "keep managed + merged MCP" vs "switch to vanilla Messages API" with concrete port scope? That's the right next gate before Karma fast-lanes anything ‚Äî you don't want to fast-lane "merge MCP into S1" if the right answer is "delete managed agent entirely".

## Sona ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:32:08Z

Services audit back. Highlights ‚Äî S1 audit still running.

### Good news: S2 is complete
- `GET /v1/schema`, `GET /v1/config/{id}`, `POST /v1/config`, `PATCH /v1/config/{id}` (versioning baked in), plus `/versions` history. All auth-wrapped. **No gap.**

### Real gaps found

1. **S3 ‚Üí S4 handoff doesn't exist.** S3 runs verification *internally* (`factory.py:verify.run_verification()`) and never POSTs to S4 `/verify`. S4 is an orphaned service ‚Äî endpoint exists but nothing calls it.
2. **S3 can't reuse a project on rebuild.** `POST /build` accepts `{sessionId, configVersion?}` only. No `projectId` to reuse an existing Wallet Studio project ‚Üí **every rebuild creates a new project**. Directly violates your iterate-same-project requirement.
3. **S5 has no fullview route.** Only `GET /v1/preview/{session_id}` exists (correctly unauthenticated for iframe). Your "Open in fullview" button has no target URL to open.
4. **S4 has no callback/webhook.** S1 would have to poll `GET /verify/{session_id}` ‚Äî there's no push path.
5. **Service-name ambiguity.** `demo-factory/` is the real S3 HTTP API; `demo-factory-cloud/` is a Slack bot and **not** the service we want. The env var currently points at `demo-factory-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app` which may be either ‚Äî worth confirming which revision is deployed.
6. **MCP `trigger_factory` targets `DEMO_STUDIO_URL/session/{sessionId}/build`** ‚Äî which is an S1 endpoint, not S3. So MCP currently calls S1, which calls S3. Extra hop that doesn't need to exist.

### What has to change in the other services

| Service | Change |
|---------|--------|
| **S3** | (a) Accept `projectId` in `POST /build` to reuse existing Wallet Studio project. (b) On build complete, POST to S4 `/verify`. (c) Record `projectId` in response so S1 can persist it in Firestore. |
| **S4** | Either add a callback/webhook to notify S1 on completion, or S1 accepts polling. Polling is simpler. |
| **S5** | Add `/v1/preview/{session_id}/fullview` route ‚Äî standalone branded page. Can be the same HTML, just served at a URL intended for direct browser navigation. |
| **MCP** | If we keep MCP at all: point `trigger_factory` at S3 directly, skip the S1 hop. (Bigger question pending ‚Äî vanilla API discussion.) |

Explore on S1 is still running ‚Äî will merge findings when that lands and then we can decide the vanilla-API-vs-MCP question with full context.

### S1 changes (what has to give)

1. **Drop brand/market from Slack `/session` trigger.** `main.py` lines 1265‚Äì1296 inject `initialContext` ‚Üí agent. Should be empty session only. (UI is where config happens.)
2. **Delete `/approve` from UI.** `studio.js` lines 646 & 839 still call `POST /session/{id}/approve`, but the route was already deleted on S1. UI ‚Üí `/build` directly.
3. **Fix or delete `/preview` iframe target.** UI at `studio.js:225` iframes `/session/{id}/preview`. Route is deleted on S1 (per BD Wave A). Either: iframe points at S5 URL directly, or S1 adds a proxy/redirect. **Simplest: iframe S5 directly**; CORS may bite ‚Äî needs verification.
4. **Fullview button target.** `studio.js:972` opens `/preview` new-tab. Should open S5's fullview route.
5. **Add `verificationStatus` field to session schema.** Currently not in `_UPDATABLE_FIELDS`. Session doc needs: `projectId`, `verificationStatus` (`pending`/`passed`/`failed`), `verificationReport` (ref to S4 result id), `lastBuildAt`.
6. **Capture `projectId` from S3 response** after build. Today `trigger_factory_v2()` is a scaffold ‚Äî nothing persists the returned projectId. Needed for iterate-same-project.
7. **Add `GET /session/{id}/logs` SSE endpoint.** Streams build progress (from S3's SSE) + verification status (polled from S4). UI consumes for the "what's happening" surface.
8. **Add S4 polling loop.** On `building ‚Üí built` transition, start polling `GET S4/verify/{sessionId}` until terminal. Write status into session doc. Stream via `/logs`.
9. **UI: gate preview iframe.** Show preview iframe only when `verificationStatus == passed` (or always-visible and just shows latest built state ‚Äî your call).
10. **UI: on rebuild from failed verification, don't reset config or projectId.** Same session, same project, new config version ‚Üí new build against same WS project.

### The "do we need MCP at all" question interacts with this

- If you **keep MCP**, you need to do the MCP `trigger_factory` rewiring (change #1 on MCP row) plus resolve the current 503 (redeploy).
- If you **switch to vanilla Messages API with client-side tools**, items 1‚Äì3 on the MCP row vanish ‚Äî MCP service deleted entirely. S1 gets the tool definitions directly: `get_schema`, `get_config`, `set_config`, `trigger_factory` as Python functions it executes locally.

Either way the S3/S4/S5/S1 changes above are required. The MCP question only affects whether `demo-studio-mcp` survives or dies.

### My read on the right next move

Before Karma fast-lanes anything, **decide the architecture question**:
- (A) Keep managed agent + merge MCP into S1 process
- (B) Ditch managed agent + vanilla Messages API with client-side tools
- (C) Keep current split; just redeploy MCP and wire the gaps

(C) is fastest to unblock today. (B) is cheapest long-term. (A) is a middle ground.

Want me to dispatch a design-assessment agent (Azir or Swain, opus) to compare (A)/(B)/(C) with concrete port scope + decision matrix, so Karma fast-lanes the right thing instead of the obvious-next thing? That's ~15‚Äì20 min of planner time and saves us from implementing the wrong architecture.

### God plan vs. constellation of small plans

**Case for god plan** (Swain/Azir writes it):
- Real dependency DAG across 4 repos. Someone needs to sequence.
- Old ship plan is outdated; having one source-of-truth for the new flow prevents drift.
- Gate for "is flow E2E live" needs to exist somewhere.

**Case against god plan** (skip it):
- Old ship plan taught us that god plans are brittle: Viktor died on cross-phase impl on a mutable branch; wave-orchestration became a month-long project.
- Each gap above is small + independent enough to ADR individually; Kayn/Aphelios breaks down per-ADR; coordinator sequences.
- Takes Swain ~45 min to author; delays actual impl by that much.

### My recommendation

**Write a lightweight god plan (~200 lines max), not a full ADR.** Its job is:
1. Name the 12 gaps.
2. Group into 4 ADRs by repo/concern (see below).
3. Sequence them with a simple dependency list.
4. Define the E2E smoke test (fresh ‚Äî the old one's scenarios are outdated).
5. Ship gate: "E2E smoke passes end-to-end on stg; flag flip on prod."

**Suggested ADR grouping:**

| ADR | Gaps | Owner | Est scope |
|-----|------|-------|-----------|
| **MCP-merge** | 1, 12 | Viktor | ~2 days |
| **S3-project-reuse + S4-trigger** | 2 | Viktor (company-os repo) | ~1 day |
| **S5-fullview** | 3 | Jayce | ~half day |
| **S1-new-flow** | 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11 | Viktor | ~3‚Äì4 days |

Then: one coordinator-side ship plan that sequences them (smaller than the old one ‚Äî maybe 150 lines).

### Answer to your question

**Yes, write a god plan, but a small one.** Ship plan v2 that:
- Supersedes the old `2026-04-21-demo-studio-v3-e2e-ship.md` (fastlaned to `implemented/` ‚Äî mark it superseded).

- Does NOT re-architect ‚Äî each ADR owns its own decisions.

## Duong ‚Äî 2026-04-21T09:41:17Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save ‚Äî Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope ‚Äî Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead ‚Äî it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty ‚Üí auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) ‚Üí coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction ‚Üí refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit ‚Äî the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** ‚Äî refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** ‚Äî Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** ‚Äî indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- Anthropic managed agents (`client.beta.agents.create` with `mcp_servers=[{type: "url", url: ...}]`)
- MCP (Model Context Protocol) ‚Äî standalone TS server vs in-process Python SDK
- Vanilla Anthropic Messages API with client-side tool execution (`tools=[...]`, `stop_reason=end_turn` loop)
- Cloud Run deploy topology: S1 demo-studio-v3, demo-studio-mcp (currently 503), S2 demo-config-mgmt, S3 demo-factory (real HTTP API) vs demo-factory-cloud (Slack bot), S4 demo-verification, S5 demo-preview
- Firestore database `demo-studio-staging` on project `mmpt-233505`, collections `demo-studio-sessions`, `configs`, `demo-studio-used-tokens`
- SE `transition_status(session_id, new_status, *, cancel_reason: str | None = None)` kwarg-only contract
- BD boundary rule: S1 = lifecycle only; S2 = config authority; thin S1‚ÜíS3 `{sessionId}` handoff; S3 self-fetches config
- MAL terminal-state hook in `transition_status` eager-terminates Anthropic managed session on `completed`/`cancelled`
- MAD dashboard tab enrichment join (Anthropic list √ó Firestore batch_get √ó S2 fetch_config)
